## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: The task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is central to constitutive modeling in solid mechanics. Stress typically increases with strain (hardening) and decreases with temperature (thermal softening), with various nonlinear coupling forms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal modulus variation)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (strain hardening in plastic regime)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition)
- Johnson-Cook flow stress (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Thermal softening linear: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (modulus linearly decreasing with temperature)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturation hardening model)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturation hardening with exponential thermal effect)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain offset)
- Exponential thermal modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal softening)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (Taylor expansion of constitutive law)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Zerilli-Armstrong BCC type: sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * T + c3 * T * log(epsilon)) (dislocation mechanics based model)
- Tanh hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (c2 + c3 * T) (smooth saturation with linear thermal factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening with saturation → 1 - exp(-c*epsilon) or tanh(c*epsilon) forms indicate dislocation density saturation
- Thermal softening → Multiplicative factor (1 - (T/Tm)^c) or exp(-c*T) representing thermally-activated dislocation mobility
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Sum of linear term (c*epsilon) and power-law term (c*epsilon^n) with n<1
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as c*T or T**c in multiplicative softening factors, reflecting fraction of melting point
- Rate-independent plasticity → sigma depends on epsilon through power-law or logarithmic forms without explicit time dependence
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 indicate thermomechanical interaction
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield strength before hardening begins
- Concave-up vs concave-down strain response → Power exponent >1 indicates geometric hardening, <1 indicates diminishing hardening rate

- `T*log(epsilon+1)`

Let me focus on candidates that have `exp(T*c)` or `exp(-c/T)` type terms AND `T*log(epsilon+1)` or equivalent.

**Candidates with `T*epsilon` terms:** `T*epsilon` ≠ `T*log(epsilon+1)` — different basis functions.

**Candidate 47:** `T^c0*c1 + T^c0*c2*epsilon^c3 + T^c0*c4*epsilon + c5*log(c6*epsilon+1) + c7 + c8*epsilon^c3 + c9*epsilon`
This has `T^c0` multiplying various epsilon terms. If c0=1, we get `T*(c1 + c2*epsilon^c3 + c4*epsilon)`. But we need `T*log(epsilon+1)`, which isn't here.

**Candidate 46:** `sqrt(T)*c0 + sqrt(T)*c1*epsilon^c2 + sqrt(T)*c3*epsilon + c4*log(c5*epsilon+1) + c6 + c7*epsilon^c2 + c8*epsilon`. Uses sqrt(T), not T or exp(-c/T).

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain both the Arrhenius term `exp(-c/T)` and the `T*log(epsilon+1)` interaction term that the GT requires. These are linearly independent basis functions that cannot be replicated by the basis functions present in any candidate.
